The Epistemological Integration of Ghayb and Shahada
Author explains Islamic epistemology linking witness and unseen via Quranic examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Quranic arguments that link observable phenomena to unseen realities and explain the epistemological function of shahada as evidence for ghayb.

Core Idea
The witnessed world is the proof for the unseen; they are integrated, not separate.

In this passage, the author shows how the Quran constantly links natural phenomena in the world of shahada (the witnessed) to realities of ghayb (the unseen) such as God, angels, the Throne, and resurrection. This integration is central to Islamic epistemology: the seen points to the unseen, and revelation supplies detailed knowledge of the unseen. By understanding this, you will grasp how the Quran uses empirical observations as rational evidence for metaphysical truths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic examples linking seen to unseen
Go through each cited verse and note what observed phenomenon (e.g., lightning, thunder, rain) is associated with which unseen reality (e.g., angels glorifying God, the Throne, resurrection).
For instance, the thunder and lightning are linked to the glorification of angels.
2
Extract the epistemological claim
From the examples, deduce the author's claim: the witnessed world provides evidence for the unseen. The author argues that all existence is in submission to God, as stated in the verses about prostration and glorification.
3
Analyze the two manifestations of integration
The author lists two aspects: (1) proofs of the unseen exist in the witnessed, and (2) creatures emerge from the unseen to the witnessed and return (birth and death). Explain how each works.
Birth and death are examples of transition between the two worlds.
4
Connect to the mission of revelation
Understand that revelation provides knowledge of the unseen to guide humans in the witnessed world, leading to integration of revelation, intellect, and the universe.
This is the author's main thesis about the recovery of Muslim intellect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثاني: الفصل الثاني- ميدان المعرفة - الغيب والشهادة
الآيات المتعلقة ببعض ظواهر الطبيعة في ميدان الآفاق من عالم الشهادة مربوطة ببعض أصناف المخلوقات في عالم الغيب كعملية تسبيح الرعد والملائكة: ﴿هُوَ الَّذِي يُرِيكُمُ الْبَرْقَ خَوْفًا وَطَمَعاً وَيُنشِئُ السَّحابَ الثّقالَ، وَيُسَبِّحُ الرَّعْدُ بِحَمْدِهِ وَالْمَلائِكَةُ مِنْ خِيفَتِهِ وَيُرْسِلُ الصَّواعِقَ فَيُصِيبُ بِها مَنْ يَشَاءُ وَهُمْ يُجادِلُونَ فِي اللهِ وَهُوَ شَدِيدُ الْمِحال (الرعد: ۱۲/۱۳-۱۳].
ويربط العرش - وهو من جنس الغيب - ببعض ظواهر الطبيعة أيضاً: ﴿ اللهُ الَّذِي رَفَعَ السَّماواتِ بِغَيْرِ عَمَدٍ تَرَوْنَهَا ثُمَّ اسْتَوَى عَلَى الْعَرْشِ وَسَخَّرَ الشَّمْسَ وَالْقَمَرَ كُلٌّ يَجْرِي لأَجَلٍ مُسَمَّى يُدَبِّرُ الأَمْرَ يُفَصِّلُ الآيَاتِ لَعَلَّكُمْ بِلِقاءِ رَبِّكُمْ تُوقِنُونَ﴾ [الرعد: ۲/۱۳].
ويستدل على البعث بمقدمات مظاهر الإحياء للنبات في ميدان الآفاق من عالم الشهادة: ﴿ ... وَتَرَى الأَرْضَ هَامِدَةً فَإِذا أَنْزَلْنَا عَلَيْها الْمَاءَ اهْتَزَّتْ وَرَبَتْ وَأَنْبَتَتْ مِنْ كُلِّ زَوْجٍ بَهِيجٍ، ذَلِكَ بِأَنَّ اللهَ هُوَ الْحَقُّ وَأَنَّهُ يُحْيِي الْمَوْتَى وَأَنَّهُ عَلَى كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَدِيرٌ، وَأَنَّ السَّاعَةَ آتِيَةٌ لا رَيْبَ فِيها وَأَنَّ اللهَ يَبْعَثُ مَنْ فِي الْقُبُور [الحج: ٥/٢٢-٧].
وجميع أجزاء الوجود غيباً كان أم شهادة ينتظم في سلك الاستسلام لله: ﴿ وَلِلَّهِ يَسْجُدُ مَنْ فِي السَّمَاواتِ وَالْأَرْضِ طَوْعاً وَكَرْهَا وَظِلالُهُمْ بِالْغُدُوِّ والآصال [الرعد: ١٥/١٣] ﴾ وَإِن مِنْ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا يُسَبِّحُ بِحَمْدِهِ وَلَكِنْ لا تَفْقَهُونَ تَسْبِيحَهُمْ ﴾ [الإسراء: ٤٤/١٧].
وأقسم الله تعالى على صدق الوحي بعالمي الغيب والشهادة مطلقاً: ﴿ فَلا أُقْسِمُ بِمَا تُبْصِرُونَ، وَما لا تُبْصِرُونَ، إِنَّهُ لَقَوْلُ رَسُولٍ كَرِيمٍ [الحاقة: ٣٨/٦٩-٤٠] ﴾
ولعلّ من أبرز مظاهر هذا التكامل بين عالم الغيب وعالم الشهادة أن أهم معطيات عالم الغيب وجود الله سبحانه وتعالى الواحد الأحد، خالق الدنيا والآخرة، وخالق الإنسان وواهبه الإرادة وحرية القرار ومسؤولية الاستخلاف في عالم الشهادة، بما أوتي من معرفة وعقل.
إن مهمة الوحي في عالم الشهادة تتمثل في إمداد الإنسان بالعلم المتصل بعالم الغيب ليربط بينه وبين هذا الإنسان في عالم الشهادة، فينشأ تكامل الوحي مع العقل والكون، ويتمكن الإنسان من تحقيق غاية وجوده في عالم الشهادة. ولن يسترد العقل المسلم عافيته إلا أن يستعيد رؤيته الإسلامية الكاملة المبنية على التوحيد والوحدانية، ليتوحد عالم الغيب مع عالم الشهادة، والوحي مع العقل والكون. وفي ضوء ما تقدم يمكن القول بأن ظاهرة التكامل بين عالمي الغيب والشهادة تبرز في مظهرين:
الأول : وجود أدلة عالم الغيب في عالم الشهادة.
الثاني: بروز المخلوقات من عالم الغيب إلى عالم الشهادة، ثم تنتقل من عالم الشهادة إلى عالم الغيب بانتظام واضطراد ومن الأمثلة على ذلك ظواهر الولادة والموت في عالم الإنسان.
وصفوة القول: إن مفهوم الغيب والشهادة في الإسلام هو المفهوم الذي يحدد معنى الحياة والوجود، وغاية الحياة والوجود وعلاقة ذلك بما وراء الحياة.
Chapter Two, Section Two: The Field of Knowledge - The Unseen and the Witnessed.
Verses related to some phenomena of nature in the field of horizons from the world of the witnessed are linked to some kinds of creatures in the world of the unseen, like the process of the glorification of thunder and the angels: 'It is He who shows you the lightning, [causing] fear and hope, and produces the heavy clouds. And the thunder exalts [Him] with praise, and the angels [as well] from fear of Him, and He sends the thunderbolts and strikes therewith whom He wills, while they dispute about Allah; and He is severe in assault.' (Ar-Ra'd 13:12-13).
And He links the Throne - which is of the kind of the unseen - with some phenomena of nature as well: 'Allah is He who raised the heavens without pillars that you can see; then He established Himself on the Throne and subjected the sun and the moon, each running for a specified term. He arranges [every] matter; He details the signs that you may, in the meeting with your Lord, be certain.' (Ar-Ra'd 13:2).
And He argues for resurrection by the precursors of the manifestations of life of vegetation in the field of horizons from the world of the witnessed: '...and you see the earth barren, but when We send down upon it rain, it quivers and swells and grows [something] of every beautiful kind. That is because Allah is the Truth, and that He gives life to the dead and that He is over all things competent. And [that] the Hour is coming – no doubt about it – and that Allah will resurrect those in the graves.' (Al-Hajj 22:5-7).
And all parts of existence, whether unseen or witnessed, are arranged in the thread of submission to Allah: 'And to Allah prostrates whoever is within the heavens and the earth, willingly or by compulsion, and their shadows [as well] in the mornings and the afternoons.' (Ar-Ra'd 13:15). 'And there is no creature but that it glorifies Him with praise, but you do not understand their glorification.' (Al-Isra' 17:44).
And Allah Almighty swore to the truth of revelation by the two worlds of the unseen and the witnessed absolutely: 'So I swear by what you see and what you do not see, [that] indeed, the Qur'an is the word of a noble Messenger.' (Al-Haqqah 69:38-40).
And perhaps one of the most prominent manifestations of this integration between the world of the unseen and the world of the witnessed is that the most important givens of the world of the unseen include the existence of Allah Almighty, the One, the Unique, Creator of this world and the Hereafter, Creator of man and the Giver to him of will, freedom of decision, and the responsibility of vicegerency in the world of the witnessed, by virtue of the knowledge and intellect he has been given.
Indeed, the mission of revelation in the world of the witnessed is to supply man with knowledge connected to the world of the unseen, in order to link it with this man in the world of the witnessed, so that an integration of revelation with intellect and the universe arises, and man can achieve the purpose of his existence in the world of the witnessed. And the Muslim intellect will not recover its health except by restoring its complete Islamic vision based on tawhid (monotheism) and uniqueness, so that the world of the unseen unites with the world of the witnessed, and revelation with intellect and the universe. In light of the foregoing, it can be said that the phenomenon of integration between the two worlds of the unseen and the witnessed appears in two aspects:
First: the existence of proofs of the world of the unseen within the world of the witnessed.
Second: the emergence of creatures from the world of the unseen into the world of the witnessed, then they move from the world of the witnessed to the world of the unseen regularly and constantly; and among the examples of that are the phenomena of birth and death in the human world.
In short: The concept of the unseen and the witnessed in Islam is the concept that defines the meaning of life and existence, the purpose of life and existence, and the relationship of that to what is beyond life.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological exposition of the Islamic concept of 'al-ghayb' (the unseen) and 'al-shahada' (the witnessed). The author begins by citing Quranic verses that link natural phenomena observable in the world of the witnessed (e.g., lightning, thunder, rain, the growth of plants) to realities of the unseen world (e.g., the glorification of thunder and angels, the Throne of Allah, resurrection). The purpose is to show that the Quran does not separate the two realms but rather uses the witnessed as signs pointing to the unseen. For instance, the verse from Surah Ar-Ra'd connects the observable process of thunder and lightning to the unseen act of angels glorifying God. Similarly, the Throne, an unseen reality, is linked to the observable heavens and celestial bodies. The most explicit argument from natural observation is the resurrection analogy: the dead earth coming to life after rain is used as a proof for the resurrection of the dead. The author then states that all existence, whether unseen or witnessed, is in submission to Allah, as per the Quranic verses about prostration and glorification. The passage also highlights an oath by Allah swearing by both the seen and the unseen to affirm the truth of revelation. The author then discusses the integration (takamul) between the two worlds, emphasizing that the most important datum from the unseen is the existence of God, and that revelation provides knowledge of the unseen to guide humans in the witnessed world. Two manifestations of this integration are given: first, that proofs of the unseen exist within the witnessed; second, that creatures emerge from the unseen to the witnessed and then return (like birth and death). Finally, the author summarizes that the Islamic concept of ghayb and shahada defines the meaning and purpose of life, linking it to the afterlife.

Key Terms
الغيب
الشهادة
التكامل

A) The rising and setting of the sun

C) The movement of clouds by the wind

Key Takeaway
The Quran integrates the witnessed world as evidence for the unseen, establishing an epistemology where visible signs lead to certain knowledge of God, the afterlife, and other metaphysical realities.

Three Definitions of the Unseen World (ʿĀlam al-Ghayb)
Author presents three definitions of the unseen world.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the three definitions of the unseen world presented in the passage and identify their key features.

Core Idea
Definitions of the unseen range from metaphysical to sensory-dependent, each with different implications.

The passage opens by acknowledging that the unseen is beyond the sensory, but then presents three more precise definitions. Each definition has a different criterion: metaphysical transcendence, divine exclusivity, and sensory inaccessibility. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for grasping the Islamic theological concept of the unseen.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first definition
Look for the first description: 'ālam al-ghayb is a rational, moral world transcending matter. Note its focus on the non-material nature and that humans only perceive its effects (e.g., God, angels, jinn).
This definition is metaphysical and absolute.
2
Identify the second definition
It describes the unseen as particular to Allah's knowledge alone, with revelation as the means of communication. This definition emphasizes divine exclusivity.
This definition is theological and centered on revelation.
3
Identify the third definition
It defines the unseen as everything hidden from customary sensory perception. This makes the unseen relative to human capacity.
This definition is sensory-based and subject to change.
4
Compare the definitions
Which definitions are absolute? Which is relative? Why does the author later critique the third? Consider how each definition would classify the same entity (e.g., jinn) differently.
The critique hinges on the third definition's dependency on human sensory capacity.

الباب الثاني: الفصل الثاني- ميدان المعرفة - الغيب والشهادة الميدان الأول الغيب التعريف: سبقت الإشارة إلى أن عالم الغيب يمثل ما وراء المحسوس إجمالاً، ولكن سعى بعض الباحثين لمحاولة وضع تعريفات جامعة ومنها: - عالم الغيب عالم ذو طبيعة عقلية معنوية متعالية عن المادة، ولذلك فإنه ليس بعالم قابل للشهود الإنساني، بل يدرك الإنسان ثبوته وآثاره فحسب كالوجود الإلهي، ووجود الملائكة والجن والجنة والنار، وغيرها من الموجودات الغيبية، والله تعالى وحده الذي يحيط علمه بعالمي الغيب والشهادة جميعاً. عالم الغيب عالم يخص به علم الله وحده، يوحي ما يشاء من أمره على من يشاء من عباده، ويرسلهم بالرسالات إلى الأمم هداية وتبصيراً لمعنى وجودهم، وغاية هذا الوجود، وعلاقته ومآله. - عالم الغيب كل أمر غائب عن مجال إدراكنا الحسي العادة. ونجد أن صاحب هذا التعريف الأخير يعود ليقرر أن مناط عالم الغيب قائم على عدم قدرتنا على مشاهدة ما غاب عن حواسنا، وعليه فإن أموراً كانت غيباً يوماً ما، ثم غدت مشاهدة لا تعدّ من عالم الغيب، بل من عالم الشهادة. ومثال ذلك أمر الجنّ إذ لو تمكن البحث العلمي عن طريق التجربة والاختبار، واستخدام بعض القوى الكونية - أن يتصل بالجنّ مثلاً اتصالاً عادياً لأصبح أمر الجن ضمن عالم الشهادة، والتي كانت فيما سبق في إطار عالم الغيب الذي سبيله الوحيد الوحي. وكذلك الحال في مثل قدرة الأبحاث الجنينية التنبؤ بما في بطن الحامل من جنس المولود، فإن هذا لم يعد غيباً، بل غدا جزءاً من عالم الشهادة. وثمة باحثون يجعلون مناط عالم الغيب قائماً على أساس انتماء كل كائن غير محسوس إليه، بحيث إن كل ما يدرك الإحساس يعدّ مادياً. والمادي هو كل ما يتكون من العناصر المادية التي استقرأها العلماء ورصدوها في الطبيعة والفضاء. ولذلك فإن عالم الغيب أو عوالم الغيب هي: السماوات الست التي تعلو السماء الدنيا، والأرضون الست، حيث تكون كل أرض وسماء عالماً مستقلاً له مخلوقاته، وناموسه، وطبيعته، وقوانينه. والأمر الجدير بالتأكيد عليه في قضية عالم الغيب في المفهوم الإسلامي عدم إفادته لمعنى الإيمان من غير دليل كما هو حاصل في مفهوم الميتافيزيقا الغربية، إذ إن طبيعة العلاقة العضوية بين عالمي الغيب والشهادة قد أبانت حقيقة أن وجود أدلة عالم الغيب متضمنة في عالم الشهادة. في ضوء تلك التعريفات بوسعنا أن نقول: إن عالم الغيب هو جميع مالا قدرة للإنسان على الإحاطة بتفصيلاته، عن طريق الحواس، على نحو قاطع.
Chapter Two: Section Two - Field of Knowledge - The Unseen and the Witnessed, The First Field: The Unseen. Definition: Reference was previously made that the world of the Unseen represents what is beyond the sensory in general, but some researchers have attempted to produce comprehensive definitions, including: - The world of the Unseen is a world of a rational, moral nature transcending matter, and therefore it is not a world subject to human witnessing, rather man perceives its existence and effects only, such as the divine existence, the existence of angels, jinn, Paradise, Hell, and other unseen beings, and Allah Almighty alone encompasses with His knowledge both the worlds of the Unseen and the Witnessed. - The world of the Unseen is a world particular to the knowledge of Allah alone; He reveals what He wills of His command to whomever He wills of His servants, and sends them with messages to the nations for guidance and insight into the meaning of their existence, the purpose of this existence, its relation and its outcome. - The world of the Unseen is every matter hidden from the scope of our customary sensory perception. And we find that the author of this last definition returns to state that the criterion of the world of the Unseen is based on our inability to observe what is hidden from our senses, and accordingly, matters that were once unseen, then became observable, are not considered part of the world of the Unseen, but rather of the world of the Witnessed. An example of that is the matter of jinn: if scientific research through experiment and testing, and the use of some cosmic forces, could establish ordinary contact with jinn, then the matter of jinn would become within the world of the Witnessed, whereas previously it was within the framework of the world of the Unseen, whose only path is revelation. Similarly, the case of the ability of embryological research to predict the gender of the fetus in the pregnant woman's womb, for this is no longer unseen, but has become part of the world of the Witnessed. And there are researchers who make the criterion of the world of the Unseen based on the affiliation of every imperceptible being to it, such that everything perceived by sensation is considered material. And the material is everything composed of the material elements that scientists have examined and observed in nature and space. Therefore, the world of the Unseen or the worlds of the Unseen are: the six heavens above the lowest heaven, and the six earths, where each earth and heaven is an independent world with its creatures, its law, its nature, and its laws. And the matter that deserves emphasis in the issue of the world of the Unseen in the Islamic concept is that it does not provide meaning of faith without evidence, as is the case in the concept of Western metaphysics, since the nature of the organic relationship between the worlds of the Unseen and the Witnessed has shown the fact that the existence of evidence for the world of the Unseen is contained within the world of the Witnessed. In light of those definitions, we can say: The world of the Unseen is all that man has no ability to comprehend its details through the senses in a definitive manner.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage defines the concept of 'ālam al-ghayb (the world of the Unseen) and critiques various definitions. The author begins by stating that previous references have described the Unseen as beyond the sensory, but researchers have attempted more comprehensive definitions. Three definitions are cited: (1) The Unseen is a rational, moral world transcending matter; humans only perceive its existence and effects, such as God, angels, jinn, etc. (2) The Unseen is particular to Allah's knowledge; He reveals what He wills through messengers. (3) The Unseen is everything hidden from sensory perception. The author notes that the third definition implies that if something becomes observable (e.g., jinn contacted scientifically, or fetal gender prediction), it moves from the Unseen to the Witnessed. Some researchers define the Unseen as everything imperceptible, equating the perceptible with the material. They then specify that the Unseen consists of multiple worlds (six heavens and six earths). The author warns that the Islamic concept of the Unseen does not posit faith without evidence, unlike Western metaphysics, because evidence for the Unseen is embedded in the Witnessed. Finally, the author summarizes: the Unseen is everything man cannot definitively comprehend through senses.

Key Terms
عالم الغيب (ʿālam al-ghayb): The world of the unseen: everything beyond human sensory perception, including God, angels, jinn, Paradise, Hell, and other non-material existents; its evidence is found in the witnessed world. [Note: In classical logic, 'ghayb' is not a technical term; here it is used in a theological-epistemological context.]
عالم الشهادة (ʿālam al-shahāda): The world of the witnessed: everything that can be perceived by the senses, including material objects and phenomena.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the three definitions makes the unseen world relative to human sensory capacity?
A) The first definition (transcendent, moral nature)
B) The second definition (particular to Allah's knowledge)
C) The third definition (hidden from customary sensory perception)
D) None of them

Key Takeaway
The three definitions of the unseen differ in their criteria: metaphysical transcendence, divine exclusivity, and sensory inaccessibility, with the last being relative.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Choose one of the definitions and explain which entities it would include or exclude compared to the other definitions.

The Islamic Critique of Sensory-Dependent Definitions of the Unseen
Author critiques the sensory-based definition and presents the Islamic alternative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Islamic concept of the unseen does not make faith dependent on sensory evidence and how evidence for the unseen is found in the witnessed world.

Core Idea
The unseen is not defined by temporary sensory inaccessibility but by inherent imperceptibility; its evidence is embedded in the material world.

The passage presents and then critiques a definition that equates the unseen with whatever is currently hidden from the senses. This definition is problematic because it would make the unseen relative and subject to change. The author then contrasts the Islamic understanding with Western metaphysics, emphasizing that the Islamic concept of the unseen is not a matter of blind faith but is supported by evidence within the witnessed world.

Guided Path
1
Understand the third definition's implication
According to the third definition, if something becomes observable (e.g., jinn contacted scientifically), it moves from unseen to witnessed. Note the relativistic consequence.
This definition ties the unseen to human sensory capacity, which changes over time.
2
Follow the author's critique
The author points out that this definition fails because it bases the unseen on sensory accessibility, which is variable. Examples: scientific contact with jinn, embryological prediction of gender.
The critique shows that such a definition cannot provide a stable metaphysical category.
3
Identify the Islamic alternative
The passage then asserts that the unseen is not temporary; it consists of multiple worlds (six heavens, six earths) with their own laws, but its evidence is contained within the witnessed world.
The Islamic concept posits an organic relationship between the two worlds.
4
Compare with Western metaphysics
Western metaphysics posits a separate realm without empirical evidence, whereas Islam sees evidence for the unseen in the witnessed world. This distinguishes Islamic epistemology.
The passage emphasizes that Islamic faith in the unseen is not baseless.

Exclusive Divine Knowledge of the Unseen: Two Quranic Characteristics
Author lists two key characteristics of the unseen world: exclusive knowledge by Allah and comprehensive scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and explain the two key characteristics of the unseen world as stated in the Quran.

Core Idea
Allah alone knows the unseen, and His knowledge covers every detail.

The Quran often speaks about the unseen world (al-ghayb) as a realm beyond human perception. This lesson focuses on two fundamental characteristics that the Quran attributes to this world: that its knowledge is exclusive to Allah and that it encompasses both the smallest and largest realities. Understanding these helps ground Islamic epistemology and the necessity of revelation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two characteristics
Read the passage and locate the two main features of the unseen world. The first is that knowledge of the unseen belongs to Allah alone. The second is that His knowledge is comprehensive, covering all particulars and universals.
2
Find the Quranic evidence for each
The passage cites two verses: Surah Al-An'am 6:73 for exclusivity ('Knower of the Unseen and the Witnessed') and Surah Saba' 34:3 for comprehensiveness (nothing escapes His knowledge, not even an atom's weight). Write down the key Arabic phrases that support each claim.
Look for the words 'عالِمُ الْغَيْبِ وَالشَّهَادَةِ' and 'مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ'.
3
Analyze the logical relationship
Consider how the two characteristics are connected. The comprehensiveness of Allah's knowledge reinforces His exclusive authority over the unseen. If His knowledge covers every detail, then no part of the unseen is accessible to others independently.
This logical connection is key to understanding why revelation is necessary for knowledge of the unseen.
4
Apply to Islamic theology
Reflect on why these characteristics matter for kalam and tafsir. For example, they affirm that prophets receive knowledge of the unseen only through revelation, not through reason alone. This is a cornerstone of Islamic epistemology.
You might recall the verse 'And of knowledge, you have been given only a little' (Al-Isra 17:85).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خصائص الغيب لعل أهم خصيصة يمتاز بها عالم الغيب في القرآن الكريم أن علمه ملك لله وحده، وقد دلّت النصوص القرآنية على ذلك في غير ما آية من كتاب الله العزيز، ومنها: عالِمُ الْغَيْبِ وَالشَّهَادَةِ وَهُوَ الْحَكِيمُ الْخَبير)) [الأنعام: ٧٣/٦). صفات عالم الغيب استغراق علمه للجزئيات والكليات معاً: ومن عالِمِ الْغَيْبِ لا يَعْزُبُ عَنْهُ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ فِي السَّمَاوَاتِ وَلَا فِي الْأَرْضِ وَلَا أَصْغَرُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ وَلا أَكْبَرُ إِلا فِي كِتَابٍ مُبِينٍ) (سبا: ٣/٣٤).
Characteristics of the Unseen. Perhaps the most important characteristic that distinguishes the world of the Unseen in the Noble Quran is that its knowledge belongs to Allah alone, and the Quranic texts have indicated that in more than one verse from the Mighty Book of Allah, including: 'Knower of the Unseen and the Witnessed, and He is the All-Wise, the All-Aware' [Al-An'am 6:73]. Attributes of the world of the Unseen: the comprehensiveness of His knowledge of both particulars and universals: and from 'Knower of the Unseen, not absent from Him is the weight of an atom in the heavens or in the earth, nor smaller than that nor larger, but in a clear Book' [Saba' 34:3].
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage lists the characteristics of the unseen world as derived from the Quran. The author identifies two key features. First, the most important characteristic: knowledge of the unseen belongs exclusively to Allah. This is supported by Quranic evidence, specifically the verse from Surah Al-An'am stating that Allah is the Knower of the unseen and the witnessed. Second, the attribute of comprehensiveness: Allah's knowledge encompasses both particulars and universals, as indicated by the verse from Surah Saba' that nothing, not even an atom's weight, escapes His knowledge. The author emphasizes that these characteristics establish the unseen as a domain of divine prerogative, distinct from human knowledge.

Key Terms
الغيب
علم

A) It is material and can be accessed by science.
B) Its knowledge belongs exclusively to Allah.
C) It is only about the six heavens and six earths.
D) It can change over time as things become known.

Key Takeaway
The Quran establishes that knowledge of the unseen is exclusive to Allah and comprehensive, forming the foundation of Islamic epistemology.

Critiquing the Division of al-Ghayb
Presents and critiques a division of the unseen into two categories based on potential observability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the flaw in a relative definition of al-ghayb and explain why an absolute definition is required in Islamic theology.

Core Idea
The unseen is not relative; it is absolutely hidden from the senses, or it is not truly ghayb.

In this passage, the author presents a proposed division of the unseen into two categories based on potential observability by different creatures. However, he immediately critiques it using a key definitional principle: the unseen must be defined as absolutely hidden from the senses to avoid confusion with conjectural matters. This lesson walks you through the division and its first critique.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of the division
Find the two parts: (1) what could become witnessed if conditions allow, and (2) what remains absolutely hidden, known only to Allah.
2
Recall the author's adopted definition of al-ghayb
The author states earlier that al-ghayb is what is absolutely hidden from the senses (ghaib 'an al-hawass 'ala nahw qati'), not relative to any observer.
This definition is meant to exclude mere conjectural matters.
3
Spot the contradiction
The first category implies that something can be unseen for one creature and witnessed for another, which conflicts with the absolute definition that requires hiddenness from all senses.
The division is based on a relative notion of ghayb.
4
Understand the critique's point
The division would include things that are not truly ghayb upon investigation, such as things that are merely unknown due to lack of conditions for observation.
Thus the division fails because it violates the adopted rigorous definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هل يُجَزا الغيب؟ يذهب بعض الباحثين إلى تجزئة الغيب بوضعه في قسمين: أحدهما : قسم قابل لأن يكون من عالم الشهادة إذا تهيأت للمخلوقات شروط مشاهدته. الآخر: قسم غير قابل لأن يكون من عالم الشهادة لأنه مما استأثر الله تعالى - بعلمه لنفسه (۱). ولعلّ دافع صاحب هذا التقسيم هو مفهومه لمعنى الغيب - وقد مر معنا - ثم تصوره لإمكان أن تكون هناك أشياء من عالم الغيب بالنسبة إلى الإنسان، لكنها قد تكون من عالم الشهادة بالنسبة إلى الجن أو الملائكة أو مخلوقات أخرى (٢) . بيد أن ثمة ملحوظتين على هذا التقسيم: الأولى: سبق أن تم تبني تعريف الغيب بما غاب عن الحواس على نحو قاطع خروجاً من الوقوع في أمور ظنية تحسب من الغيب، وماهي من الغيب عند التحقيق في أمرها.
Is the unseen divided? Some researchers go to dividing the unseen by placing it into two sections: One: a section that can be from the world of witnessing if the conditions for its observation become available to creatures. The other: a section that cannot be from the world of witnessing because it is what Allah has exclusively kept knowledge of for Himself. Perhaps the motive of the proponent of this division is his concept of the meaning of the unseen - which has already passed with us - then his conception of the possibility that there are things from the world of the unseen relative to humans, but they may be from the world of witnessing relative to jinn, angels, or other creatures. However, there are two observations on this division: The first: The definition of the unseen has already been adopted as what is absolutely hidden from the senses, to avoid falling into conjectural matters that are considered from the unseen but are not from the unseen upon investigation.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage is critical, presenting a proposed division of the unseen (al-ghayb) into two categories and then offering a critique. The division: (1) things that could become witnessed if conditions allow, and (2) things that remain absolutely unseen because Allah has kept them exclusively to Himself. The author suggests the motive for this division is a relative understanding of the unseen—what is unseen for humans might be witnessed for other beings like jinn or angels. However, the author critiques this with the first observation: the definition of the unseen adopted earlier is 'what is absolutely hidden from the senses' (ghaib 'an al-hawass 'ala nahw qati'). This definition excludes conjectural matters that might be mistaken for unseen but are not truly unseen upon investigation. Thus, the division is problematic because it relies on a relative notion rather than an absolute one. The second observation is not completed in this passage (likely continues on next page).

Key Terms
الغيب
الشهادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the unseen is always relative
B) Because the first category is actually witnessed
C) Because the definition of the unseen adopted is absolute hiddenness from senses
D) Because the division is based on Greek philosophy

Key Takeaway
The unseen must be defined as absolutely hidden from the senses to avoid relativism; otherwise, conjectural matters could be mistaken for ghayb.

Defining al-Ghayb: The Unseen in Islamic Epistemology
Author defines the unseen and emphasizes its unity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-ghayb according to the author and explain its unity despite diverse manifestations.

Core Idea
The unseen is a single reality hidden from the senses, not a fragmented realm.

How do Islamic scholars define the unseen? In this passage, the author gives a clear definition and emphasizes its unity. Understanding this definition is crucial for distinguishing between what can be known through reason and sense and what requires revelation.

Guided Path
1
Locate the Author's Definition
Find the phrase where the author defines al-ghayb: 'على نحو قاطع' indicates decisiveness. The definition is: 'كل ما غاب عن الحواس على نحو قاطع'.
2
Identify What al-Ghayb Is Not
The author criticizes a classification that includes non-human creatures. This shows that al-ghayb is not about other beings but about human knowledge of what is hidden.
3
Explain the Unity of al-Ghayb
Although al-ghayb has multiple types and manifestations, the author insists it revolves within the framework of a universal concept. This unity is important for epistemology.
4
Contrast with al-Shahadah
Al-ghayb is what is hidden, while al-shahadah is the witnessed world. This contrast is fundamental in Islamic thought.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثاني: الفصل الثاني- ميدان المعرفة - الغيب والشهادة
الثانية: إن الباحث صاحب هذا التقسيم يُدخل مخلوقات غير الإنسان في مسألة المعرفة مع أن مدار بحثنا هنا هو المعرفة لدى الإنسان، لما يمتاز به عن سائر الكائنات، وعليه فإن هذا التقسيم غير ذي موضوع بالنسبة إلى هذه الدراسة على الأقل. ويبقى التأكيد على وحدة عالم الغيب وكليته، وعدم تجزئته على تلك الصورة، فالغيب وإن تعددت أنواعه و تشعبت مظاهره، فإن هذا التنوع وذلك التشعب يدور في إطار المفهوم الكلّي للغيب، ليس أكثر .
أدوات معرفة الغيب
وإذا كان معنى الغيب كل ما غاب عن الحواس على نحو قاطع، فهل يعني ذلك أن أدوات المعرفة الحسية والعقلية مما لا مجال لها في ميدان الغيب؟. والجواب يتطلب قدراً من التفصيل.
وهنا يحسن التأكيد على أنه من المتعذر على أيّ من الحس أو العقل الحصول على معرفة ما إلا عن طريقهما معاً - إلا إذا استثنينا قوانين العقل الأوليـة التـي سيرد التفصيل فيها في المقام المناسب من هذه الدراسة - وعلى هذا نتفهم كيف العلاقة بين عالم الغيب وعالم الشهادة يشير إلى إمكان أن تستخدم أن حجم كل من أداتي الحس والعقل فيهما معا. فمنهج المعرفة في عالم الغيب ينطلق من مدركات حسية متجاوزاً الإطار المادي المحدود، ليتفاعل مع المبادئ الأولية للعقل، فيتمكن من إدراك قضايا الغيب الكبرى من ألوهية وربوبية وأسماء وصفات ونبوة على نحو من المعرفة العلمية (۱) ، المستندة إلى نصوص الوحي. وكذلك العقل فإن بإمكان النظر العقلي معرفة بعض الكليات العقدية كوجود الله تعالى – من حيث مبدأ التسليم - ومعرفة النبوة، بوصفها طريقاً للمعرفة الغيبية (٢) . ولكن أياً من الحس أو العقل لا يقوى على أن يصل إلى معرفة تفصيلية عن عالم الغيب لأن طريق ذلك هو الوحي فحسب، وسواء حاول أي منهما أن يستقل بذاته في هذه المعرفة، أم تكاملاً معاً فإن النتيجة في عدم الوصول إلى شيء من المعرفة التفصيلية واحدة.
The second [point]: The researcher who made this classification includes non-human creatures in the issue of knowledge while our focus here is human knowledge, due to its distinction from other beings. Therefore, this classification is irrelevant to this study at least. The emphasis remains on the unity and totality of the unseen world, and its non-fragmentation in that form. For the unseen, even if its types are multiple and its manifestations diverse, this diversity and that multiplicity revolve within the framework of the universal concept of the unseen, nothing more.

Tools for knowing the unseen
If the meaning of the unseen is everything that is decisively hidden from the senses, does that mean that the sensory and rational tools of knowledge have no place in the domain of the unseen? The answer requires a degree of detail.
Here it is good to emphasize that it is impossible for either sense or reason to obtain any knowledge except through both of them together - except if we exclude the primary laws of reason, which will be detailed in the appropriate place in this study. And on this basis we understand how the relationship between the world of the unseen and the world of testimony indicates the possibility that the extent of each of the two tools, sense and reason, is used in both. So the method of knowledge in the world of the unseen starts from sensory perceptions, transcending the limited material framework, to interact with the primary principles of reason, enabling the perception of major issues of the unseen such as divinity, lordship, names and attributes, and prophethood, in a manner of scientific knowledge (1), based on the texts of revelation. Likewise, the intellect, for rational reflection can know some theological universals such as the existence of God Almighty - in terms of the principle of submission - and knowledge of prophethood, as a path to knowledge of the unseen (2). But neither sense nor reason is able to arrive at detailed knowledge of the unseen world because the path to that is revelation alone. And whether either of them attempts to be independent in this knowledge, or both together, the result is identical: not arriving at any detailed knowledge.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage defines the domain of the unseen (al-ghayb) and discusses the epistemological tools for knowing it. It begins by refuting a classification that includes non-human creatures, asserting the unity of the unseen. Then it defines al-ghayb as what is decisively hidden from the senses. The author then addresses whether sense and reason can be used in this domain. He argues that sense and reason must work together for knowledge, except for primary rational principles. The method in the unseen world starts with sensory perceptions and interacts with rational principles, leading to knowledge of theological issues based on revelation. Reason can know some universals, but detailed knowledge of the unseen requires revelation alone. Both tools together cannot achieve detailed knowledge. This emphasizes the epistemological role of revelation as the sole source for detailed knowledge of the unseen. The author uses examples from Islamic theology such as divinity, prophethood, and attributes.

Key Terms
الغيب (al-ghayb): Everything that is decisively hidden from the senses. [Note: No significant shift.]
الشهادة (al-shahadah): The witnessed world accessible to the senses. [Note: No significant shift.]
الحس (al-hiss): Sensory perception, one of the two main tools of knowledge. [Note: No significant shift.]
العقل (al-'aql): Intellect/reason, the other main tool of knowledge, including primary rational principles. [Note: No significant shift.]
الوحي (al-wahy): Revelation, the exclusive source for detailed knowledge of the unseen. [Note: No significant shift.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the definition of al-ghayb?
A) Everything that is unknown until revelation.
B) Everything decisively hidden from the senses.
C) The world of jinn and angels only.
D) Everything that reason cannot grasp.

Key Takeaway
Al-ghayb is a single, unified reality defined by its absolute hiddenness from the senses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using the author's definition, classify the following as al-ghayb or al-shahadah: the existence of angels, the physical appearance of the Prophet (peace be upon him), the Day of Judgment. Justify each based on whether they are 'decisively hidden from the senses'.

The Cooperative Role of Sense and Reason in Knowledge of the Unseen
Author explains how sense and reason cooperate in knowing the unseen.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how sense and reason work together to attain knowledge of the unseen, and identify the exception of primary rational principles.

Core Idea
Sense and reason are interdependent; neither alone can access the unseen, but together they can grasp its major themes through revelation.

The author argues that sense and reason must cooperate for any knowledge, except for primary rational principles. How then can we know about God, prophethood, and the afterlife? The answer lies in their synergy, grounded in revelation.

Guided Path
1
Find the Author's Statement on Interdependence
Locate the phrase: 'من المتعذر على أيّ من الحس أو العقل الحصول على معرفة ما إلا عن طريقهما معاً'. This states that neither can obtain knowledge without the other.
2
Identify the Exception
The author excludes 'قوانين العقل الأولية' (primary laws of reason) from this rule. These are self-evident principles like the law of non-contradiction.
3
Describe the Method in the Unseen World
The method starts with sensory perceptions, then interacts with rational principles, and is based on revelation. Example: knowledge of divinity and prophethood.
4
Recognize the Limits
Even together, sense and reason cannot reach detailed knowledge; that requires revelation alone.

Source Text

5 min
Revelation as the Exclusive Source for Detailed Knowledge of the Unseen
Author asserts revelation as the only source for detailed unseen knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the limits of sense and reason and the exclusive role of revelation in providing detailed knowledge of the unseen.

Core Idea
Only revelation gives detailed knowledge of the unseen—sense and reason together cannot achieve it.

The author concludes that neither sense nor reason, individually or together, can provide detailed knowledge of the unseen. This underscores the necessity of revelation. Why is this important? It establishes the epistemological authority of the Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Find the Author's Conclusion
Locate the statement: 'ولكن أياً من الحس أو العقل لا يقوى على أن يصل إلى معرفة تفصيلية عن عالم الغيب لأن طريق ذلك هو الوحي فحسب'.
2
Identify the Exclusive Source
The word 'الوحي فحسب' (revelation alone) indicates exclusivity. No other tool can provide details.
3
Consider the Combined Effort
The author says even if both sense and reason cooperate ('أم تكاملاً معاً'), the result is the same: no detailed knowledge.
4
Apply to Islamic Theology
Think of examples like the exact description of Paradise, which are known only through the Quran and hadith.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثاني: الفصل الثاني- ميدان المعرفة - الغيب والشهادة
الثانية: إن الباحث صاحب هذا التقسيم يُدخل مخلوقات غير الإنسان في مسألة المعرفة مع أن مدار بحثنا هنا هو المعرفة لدى الإنسان، لما يمتاز به عن سائر الكائنات، وعليه فإن هذا التقسيم غير ذي موضوع بالنسبة إلى هذه الدراسة على الأقل. ويبقى التأكيد على وحدة عالم الغيب وكليته، وعدم تجزئته على تلك الصورة، فالغيب وإن تعددت أنواعه و تشعبت مظاهره، فإن هذا التنوع وذلك التشعب يدور في إطار المفهوم الكلّي للغيب، ليس أكثر .
أدوات معرفة الغيب
وإذا كان معنى الغيب كل ما غاب عن الحواس على نحو قاطع، فهل يعني ذلك أن أدوات المعرفة الحسية والعقلية مما لا مجال لها في ميدان الغيب؟. والجواب يتطلب قدراً من التفصيل.
وهنا يحسن التأكيد على أنه من المتعذر على أيّ من الحس أو العقل الحصول على معرفة ما إلا عن طريقهما معاً - إلا إذا استثنينا قوانين العقل الأوليـة التـي سيرد التفصيل فيها في المقام المناسب من هذه الدراسة - وعلى هذا نتفهم كيف العلاقة بين عالم الغيب وعالم الشهادة يشير إلى إمكان أن تستخدم أن حجم كل من أداتي الحس والعقل فيهما معا. فمنهج المعرفة في عالم الغيب ينطلق من مدركات حسية متجاوزاً الإطار المادي المحدود، ليتفاعل مع المبادئ الأولية للعقل، فيتمكن من إدراك قضايا الغيب الكبرى من ألوهية وربوبية وأسماء وصفات ونبوة على نحو من المعرفة العلمية (۱) ، المستندة إلى نصوص الوحي. وكذلك العقل فإن بإمكان النظر العقلي معرفة بعض الكليات العقدية كوجود الله تعالى – من حيث مبدأ التسليم - ومعرفة النبوة، بوصفها طريقاً للمعرفة الغيبية (٢) . ولكن أياً من الحس أو العقل لا يقوى على أن يصل إلى معرفة تفصيلية عن عالم الغيب لأن طريق ذلك هو الوحي فحسب، وسواء حاول أي منهما أن يستقل بذاته في هذه المعرفة، أم تكاملاً معاً فإن النتيجة في عدم الوصول إلى شيء من المعرفة التفصيلية واحدة.
The second [point]: The researcher who made this classification includes non-human creatures in the issue of knowledge while our focus here is human knowledge, due to its distinction from other beings. Therefore, this classification is irrelevant to this study at least. The emphasis remains on the unity and totality of the unseen world, and its non-fragmentation in that form. For the unseen, even if its types are multiple and its manifestations diverse, this diversity and that multiplicity revolve within the framework of the universal concept of the unseen, nothing more.

Tools for knowing the unseen
If the meaning of the unseen is everything that is decisively hidden from the senses, does that mean that the sensory and rational tools of knowledge have no place in the domain of the unseen? The answer requires a degree of detail.
Here it is good to emphasize that it is impossible for either sense or reason to obtain any knowledge except through both of them together - except if we exclude the primary laws of reason, which will be detailed in the appropriate place in this study. And on this basis we understand how the relationship between the world of the unseen and the world of testimony indicates the possibility that the extent of each of the two tools, sense and reason, is used in both. So the method of knowledge in the world of the unseen starts from sensory perceptions, transcending the limited material framework, to interact with the primary principles of reason, enabling the perception of major issues of the unseen such as divinity, lordship, names and attributes, and prophethood, in a manner of scientific knowledge (1), based on the texts of revelation. Likewise, the intellect, for rational reflection can know some theological universals such as the existence of God Almighty - in terms of the principle of submission - and knowledge of prophethood, as a path to knowledge of the unseen (2). But neither sense nor reason is able to arrive at detailed knowledge of the unseen world because the path to that is revelation alone. And whether either of them attempts to be independent in this knowledge, or both together, the result is identical: not arriving at any detailed knowledge.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage defines the domain of the unseen (al-ghayb) and discusses the epistemological tools for knowing it. It begins by refuting a classification that includes non-human creatures, asserting the unity of the unseen. Then it defines al-ghayb as what is decisively hidden from the senses. The author then addresses whether sense and reason can be used in this domain. He argues that sense and reason must work together for knowledge, except for primary rational principles. The method in the unseen world starts with sensory perceptions and interacts with rational principles, leading to knowledge of theological issues based on revelation. Reason can know some universals, but detailed knowledge of the unseen requires revelation alone. Both tools together cannot achieve detailed knowledge. This emphasizes the epistemological role of revelation as the sole source for detailed knowledge of the unseen. The author uses examples from Islamic theology such as divinity, prophethood, and attributes.

Key Terms
الوحي (al-wahy): Revelation, the exclusive source for detailed knowledge of the unseen. [Note: No significant shift.]
معرفة تفصيلية (ma'rifa tafsiliyya): Detailed knowledge, as opposed to general or universal knowledge. [Note: No significant shift.]

B) Reason alone.
C) Both sense and reason together.
D) Revelation alone.

Key Takeaway
Detailed knowledge of the unseen is exclusively attainable through revelation, not through sense or reason.

Distinguishing Sensualism and Empiricism through Tasawwur and Tasdiq
Comparison of empiricism and sensualism linked to tasawwur and tasdiq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate between the sensualist and empiricist schools of knowledge by mapping them to the logical domains of tasawwur and tasdiq.

Core Idea
Sensualism feeds concepts; empiricism judges reality.

In this passage, the author compares two epistemological schools—sensualism (ḥissiyya) and empiricism (tajribiyya)—and links them to the foundational logical distinction between tasawwur (concept formation) and tasdiq (assent). Understanding this mapping sharpens your ability to classify sources of knowledge in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common ground
Both schools agree that external perception through the senses is the origin of all knowledge. Locate this commonality in the Arabic passage.
The phrase 'بجامع التقاء الطرفين في اعتبار الإدراك الخارجي' indicates shared foundation.
2
Distinguish the schools
Sensualism holds that all knowledge is based on sense perception and then transferred to the intellect. Empiricism holds that experience (tajriba) through sensory perceptions is the sole source. Find the precise formulation in the text.
The author says 'المذهب الحسي يعدّ جميع المعارف قائمة على إدراك الحواس' vs 'الاتجاه التجريبي يعد التجربة مصدراً وحيداً للمعرفة'.
3
Map to tasawwur and tasdiq
The author states that sensualism falls within the domain of tasawwur (concept formation) because it involves forming mental images from sensory input. Empiricism falls within tasdiq (assent/judgment) because it involves affirming or denying propositions based on experience.
Look for 'تدخل في محال التصور' and 'تدخل في محال التصديق'.
4
Recognize the role of observation and experiment
Sensation comprises both passive observation (mulāḥaẓa) and active experimentation (tajriba). Note the difference: observation watches nature as is, experiment involves researcher intervention.
The author says 'الملاحظة تقتصر على مشاهدة الأشياء على ما هي عليه في الطبيعة' while 'لابد أن يتدخل الباحث في مجال بحث التجربة'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولكن لئن أرجع التجريبيون المعرفة إلى التجربة، وسواء كان ذلك مصدراً وحيداً للمعرفة، أم أساساً لها على الأقل، فذلك أيضاً هو مذهب الحسيين بجامع التقاء الطرفين في اعتبار الإدراك الخارجي، أي عن طريق الحواس أصل كل علم، ولكن لكون الحس أمراً يشمل الحواس الظاهرة والباطنة، فإن إدراك الأشياء الخارجية يسمى إحساساً، في حين يسمى إدراك الأشياء الباطنة تأملاً (۱). والتعبير الأدق أن المذهب الحسي يعدّ جميع المعارف قائمة على إدراك الحواس، ومن ثم ينقلها إلى العقل، أما الاتجاه التجريبي فيعد التجربة مصدراً وحيداً للمعرفة، وذلك من خلال المدركات الحسية. ومن هنا ندرك الصلة بين الحسية والتجريبية من زاوية كون الأولى تدخل في محال التصور، في حين تدخل الأخرى في محال التصديق()، مع الأخذ في الاعتبار أن الحس يقوم على عنصري الملاحظة والتجربة، والفرق بينهما أن الملاحظة تقتصر على مشاهدة الأشياء على ما هي عليه في الطبيعة، بينما لابد أن يتدخل الباحث في مجال بحث التجربة (۳).
But if the empiricists trace knowledge to experience, whether that is the sole source of knowledge or at least its basis, then that is also the doctrine of the sensualists due to the common ground of both parties in considering external perception, i.e., through the senses, as the origin of all knowledge. However, since sensation encompasses the external and internal senses, the perception of external things is called sensation, while the perception of internal things is called reflection (1). The more precise expression is that the sensualist school considers all knowledge to be based on sense perception, and then transfers it to the intellect, whereas the empirical school considers experience as the sole source of knowledge, through sensory perceptions. Hence we grasp the connection between sensualism and empiricism from the angle that the former falls within the domain of concepts (tasawwur), while the latter falls within the domain of assent (tasdiq), taking into account that sensation is based on two elements: observation and experiment, the difference between them being that observation is limited to watching things as they are in nature, while the researcher must intervene in the field of experiment (3).
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage compares the empiricist and sensualist schools of knowledge. The author begins by stating that both schools agree that external perception through the senses is the origin of all knowledge. He then distinguishes between sensation (external perception) and reflection (internal perception). The precise distinction is that sensualism holds all knowledge is based on sense perception and then transferred to the intellect, while empiricism holds experience (through sensory perception) as the sole source. The author then relates this to the logical concepts of tasawwur (concept formation) and tasdiq (assent or judgment): sensualism falls under tasawwur because it deals with the formation of concepts from sensory input, while empiricism falls under tasdiq because it involves judgments based on experience. Finally, he notes that sensation comprises observation (passive watching) and experiment (active intervention), and explains the difference between them.

Key Terms
تجريبي
حسي
تصور
تصديق
ملاحظة
تجربة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Sensualism (الحسية)
C) Rationalism (العقلانية)
D) Transcendentalism (المتعالية)

Key Takeaway
Sensualism corresponds to concept formation (tasawwur) and empiricism to judgment (tasdiq), a crucial distinction for Islamic epistemology.

Observation vs. Experiment in the Sensualist Framework
Explanation of observation and experiment as components of sensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between passive observation (mulāḥaẓa) and active experiment (tajriba) as components of sensation, and explain their roles in knowledge acquisition.

Core Idea
Observation watches; experiment intervenes.

The author notes that sensation comprises two elements: observation and experiment. While both are part of the sensualist method, they differ in the researcher's involvement. Understanding this distinction is crucial for evaluating how empirical claims are validated in Islamic sciences such as medicine and natural philosophy.

Guided Path
1
Define sensation as the basis of knowledge
According to sensualism, all knowledge starts from sensation (ḥiss). Locate where the author states that sensation is the foundation.
The text says 'الحس يقوم على عنصري الملاحظة والتجربة'.
2
Identify the two components
The author explicitly names observation (mulāḥaẓa) and experiment (tajriba) as the two elements of sensation.
Look for 'عنصري الملاحظة والتجربة'.
3
Understand observation
Observation is defined as watching things as they occur in nature without intervention. The researcher is a passive observer.
The phrase 'الملاحظة تقتصر على مشاهدة الأشياء على ما هي عليه في الطبيعة' is key.
4
Understand experiment
Experiment requires the researcher to actively intervene in the natural process to study phenomena under controlled conditions.
The text says 'لابد أن يتدخل الباحث في مجال بحث التجربة'.
5
Apply to Islamic sciences
Consider examples from classical Islamic medicine: observing the healing properties of honey is observation; varying dosages to determine efficacy is experiment.
Ibn Sīnā's al-Qānūn distinguishes between simple observation and systematic testing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The author begins by stating that both schools agree that external perception through the senses is the origin of all knowledge. The Conditions for Certain Sensory Knowledge in the Quranic View
Author discusses conditions for certain sensory knowledge and its limitations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three conditions the author requires for sensory testimony to yield certain knowledge and assess whether a given sensory claim meets them.

Core Idea
Sensory knowledge is valuable but never absolute; reliable only when recurrent, consistent, and rational.

The Quran honours the senses, but not as infallible sources. This lesson unpacks the exact conditions that make sensory testimony certain and shows why so many everyday perceptions fail them. You will learn to distinguish when your senses are trustworthy and when they deceive you.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions for certainty
Find in the passage the three conditions the author sets for sensory testimony (shahadat al-hiss) to be considered certain: recurrence (tawatur), agreement among different senses, and non-contradiction with rational principles.
The author calls this 'certain sensory knowledge' and contrasts it with lower degrees of certainty.
2
Analyse the principle of relative blindness
Understand the author's argument that what we cannot see far exceeds what we can see, making relative blindness a universal trait. This illustrates the inherent limitation of sight.
The author generalises this relativity to all five senses.
3
Examine Ibn Hazm's examples of sensory error
Read the quotes from Ibn Hazm showing how people mistake identities from afar, misidentify scents, and err in taste despite strong conviction. These examples demonstrate that even confident sensory reports can be wrong.
Ibn Hazm's examples highlight that sensory illusions can lead to false oaths and stubbornness.
4
Evaluate the empirical evidence for sensory deception
Consider the psychological experiment with the happy face and the classic stick-in-water illusion. How do these illustrate that our senses can be systematically deceived?
The author uses these to argue that sensory knowledge is fallible and limited.
5
Draw the epistemic conclusion
Synthesize the lesson: sensory knowledge is not absolute; it is conditionally reliable. The Quranic perspective does not reject the senses but places conditions on their trustworthiness.
This aligns with Quranic epistemology, which cautions against overreliance on sense perception alone.

Source Text

على الرغم من تلك الأهمية التي يوليها القرآن للحواس عند الإنسان، إلا أن ذلك لا يعني إطلاقية قدرات الحواس، بحيث تصبح مصدراً للمعرفة أو أداة لها على نحو يخلو من النزاع. ذلك أن المعرفة الحسية اليقينية هي التي تقدم شهادة الحس مؤكدة قاطعة عندما تتواتر شهادات الحس هذه، وتتفق مع الحواس الأخرى، ولا تتعارض مع أصول العقل وقوانينه الأولية كما سبقت الإشارة أما عندما تنزل عن هذا المستوى فإن قيمتها المعرفية تتراجع إلى ما دونها حتى آخر مرتبة الظن المرجوح. إن أحد الناس بصراً لا يتمكن من رؤية ما هو موجود إلا قدراً يسيراً بالنظر إلى ما لا يستطيع رؤيته. فهو يملك من البصر بمقدار ما يرى ولديه من العمى بمقدار ما لا يستطيع رؤيته، وعليه فإن نسبة العمى عند كل المبصرين أعظم بكثير من نسبة البصر الذي يملكونه، كما أن كل المبصرين من المخلوقين لديهم عمى نسبي بمقدار ما لا يستطيعون رؤيته من الأشياء. وهكذا النسبية في جميع الحواس. وهذا ابن حزم الأندلسي (ت:٤٥٦هـ) يعرض للاضطراب الذي قد يحصل لمن تكافأت عنده الأدلة، فينقلب إلى ضدّ ما كان يعتقده من قبل، ليهلك في سبيل إبطال ما كان يعتقده من قبل فيقول .... وهذا يعرض فيما يدرك بالحواس كثيراً، فيرى الإنسان شخصاً من بعيد فيظنه فلاناً، ويحلف عليه ويكابر ويجرد، ثم يتبين له أنه ليس هو الذي ظن، وقد يشمّ الإنسان رائحة يظنها من بعض الروائح، ويقطع على ذلك ويحلف عليه ومجدّاً، ثم يتبين لـه أنـه ليـس هـو الذي ظنّ، وهكذا في الذوق أيضاً. ويشير بعض الباحثين إلى أن الباحث - أي باحث- يجتهد في تسجيل المعلومات التي يصل إليها من الحواس، ولكنه يدرك أن أعضاء الحس في الإنسان محدودة في مداها وفي قدرتها على التمييز . بل إنه لو كان لدى الباحث كلب فإن لدى هذا الكلب من القدرة الحسية ما يؤهله لسماع نغمات صفارة لا يسمعها الباحث وزملاء الباحث قد يستطيعون السماع لمدى أكبر مما يستطيعه هو. ليس ذلك فحسب، بل إن إدراكه الحسي يختلف وفقاً للأحوال التي يمرّ بها. أي إنّ الصوت أو الطعم أو الرائحة يختلف من وقت لآخر تبعاً لحواسه التي هي عرضة للتعب أو الكيف. وإذا كان ذلك في السمع فإن أمر البصر كذلك محدود. فمما ثبت بالتجربة النفسية أنه تم عرض رسم تخطيطي لوجه رجل لا يعبر عن شيء على شاشة أمام عشرين شخصاً. وبعد أن شاهدوا كلمة (سعيد) تعرض على فترات متفاوتة تحت الصور، ظنوا أن وجه الرجل أصبح تدريجياً أكثر سعادة على الرغم من أنه لم يتغير. وهكذا فإننا عرضة للخداع البصري مما يقودنا إلى استنتاجات خاطئة عن طريق الوهم والخداع في أكثر من موقف. وما يزال المثال التقليدي حول العصا عندما تبدو في الماء منحنية في حين أنها مستقيمة عند لمسها من أكثر الاستشهادات حضوراً على خداع الحواس. إن الحواس الخمس لا تستطيع الإحاطة بكل شيء، ولو قدر لأي من الناس امتلاك غير هذه الحاسة فلربما اكتشف أشياء كثيرة مغيبة عنا الآن، لكننا لا نحس بها حيث ليس لدينا الحاسة الخاصة بإدراكها واكتشافها. إن مقياس أو مقاييس درجة الحرارة أو الضغط الجوي أو مقادير الكثافة تشهد بأن ثمة نقصاً كبيراً في حواسنا. ولو قدر لأي منا القدرة على الإحساس بهذه الظواهر لكانت حواسنا أوسع مما عليه الحال الآن. وقد اكتشف العلم
Despite the importance that the Quran gives to the senses for humans, that does not mean the absoluteness of the capacities of the senses, such that they become a source of knowledge or a tool for it in a way that is free from dispute. That is because certain sensory knowledge is that which presents the testimony of sense as confirmed and decisive when these testimonies of sense are recurrent, and agree with the other senses, and do not contradict the principles of reason and its primary laws, as previously indicated. But when it falls below this level, its cognitive value declines to below it, until the lowest rank of weak conjecture. One of the people, with sight, cannot see what exists except a small amount compared to what he cannot see. He possesses as much sight as he sees, and he has blindness to the extent he cannot see. Therefore, the proportion of blindness among all seeing people is much greater than the proportion of sight they possess, and all seeing creatures have relative blindness to the extent of what they cannot see of things. This relativity applies to all the senses. And Ibn Hazm al-Andalusi (d. 456 AH) describes the confusion that may occur to one for whom evidence is balanced, so he turns to the opposite of what he previously believed, to perish in the way of invalidating what he previously believed, saying: ... This occurs frequently in what is perceived by the senses: a person sees a person from afar and thinks he is so-and-so, and swears an oath and argues emphatically, then it becomes clear to him that he is not who he thought; and a person smells a scent he thinks is some smell, and affirms it and swears an oath insistently, then it becomes clear to him that it is not what he thought; and similarly with taste. Some researchers indicate that the researcher — any researcher — strives to record the information he reaches from the senses, but he realizes that the sense organs in humans are limited in their range and in their ability to discriminate. Indeed, if the researcher had a dog, this dog would have sensory ability enabling it to hear whistle tones that the researcher cannot hear; and colleagues of the researcher might be able to hear a greater range than he can. Not only that, but his sensory perception varies according to the conditions he undergoes. That is, sound, taste, or smell differs from time to time depending on his senses, which are subject to fatigue or condition. If that is the case for hearing, then the matter of sight is similarly limited. It has been established by psychological experiment that a schematic drawing of a man's face expressing nothing was displayed on a screen in front of twenty people. After they saw the word 'happy' displayed at intervals under the images, they thought the man's face gradually became happier, despite it having not changed. Thus we are subject to visual deception leading us to false conclusions through illusion and deception in more than one situation. The traditional example of the stick appearing bent in water while being straight when touched remains one of the most cited examples of sensory deception. The five senses cannot encompass everything, and if any person were to possess a sense other than these, perhaps they would discover many things hidden from us now, but we do not sense them because we do not have the specific sense to perceive and discover them. The thermometer or barometer or density measurements testify that there is a great deficiency in our senses. And if any of us had the ability to sense these phenomena, our senses would be wider than they are now. And science has discovered
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage discusses the epistemic status of sensory perception from a Quranic perspective, arguing that the Quran does not grant absolute authority to the senses. The author begins by acknowledging the Quranic emphasis on the senses but immediately qualifies it: this emphasis does not render the senses infallible or absolute sources of knowledge. Certain sensory knowledge is only achieved when multiple sense testimonies are recurrent, consistent with other senses, and not contradictory to primary rational principles. When these conditions are not met, the cognitive value degrades even to the level of weak conjecture. The author then illustrates the relativity of sight: a seeing person possesses a small amount of sight compared to the vastness of what they cannot see, so relative blindness is greater than sight. This relativity applies to all senses. The author quotes Ibn Hazm to show how sensory errors occur: a person may mistake a person from afar and swear to it, then discover the error; similarly with smell and taste. The author further notes that human sense organs are limited in range and discrimination, giving the example of a dog hearing frequencies humans cannot. Moreover, sensory perception varies with conditions such as fatigue. Visual deception is demonstrated by a psychological experiment where a neutral face was perceived as happier due to the subliminal word 'happy'. The classic example of the stick appearing bent in water is cited. The passage concludes that our five senses are insufficient to perceive all phenomena, and scientific instruments reveal our limitations. The overall argument is that sensory knowledge is valuable but relative, limited, and prone to error, aligning with Quranic epistemology that cautions against absolute reliance on senses.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Sensory knowledge is certain only when its testimonies are frequent, cross-validated by other senses, and rationally coherent; otherwise, it descends into conjecture.

Three Quranic Meanings of the Heart (Qalb)
Author enumerates three Quranic meanings of qalb.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the three Quranic meanings of 'qalb' (heart) as enumerated in the passage.

Core Idea
The Quran uses 'heart' for intellect, opinion, and the physical organ—three distinct meanings.

The passage opens by stating that 'qalb' in the Quran carries three distinct meanings, each supported by a specific verse. This lesson will help you recognize these meanings and their Quranic evidence, a foundational skill for understanding Quranic epistemology and tafsir.

Guided Path
1
Extract the three meanings
List the three meanings the author provides: intellect ('aql), opinion/management (ra'y/tadbir), and the physical heart in the chest. Note the Quranic verses cited for each: Qaf 50:37, al-Hashr 59:14, and al-Hajj 22:46.
2
Analyze the evidence
For each meaning, identify the verse and explain how it demonstrates that meaning. For example, Qaf 50:37 links having a 'heart' to understanding (dhikra), indicating intellect. Al-Hashr 59:14 describes hearts as scattered (shatta), referring to opinions.
The third meaning is clarified by the following discussion on basira.
3
Test the classification
Consider if any verse could be interpreted under more than one meaning. The passage notes that the third meaning also points to the functional aspect of intellect, suggesting overlap.
4
Compare with common usage
Contrast these Quranic meanings with the common contemporary association of heart with emotion only. The passage explicitly addresses this misconception later.
This step prepares for the next lesson on heart as knowledge instrument.

ويرد القلب في القرآن بمعنى من المعاني الثلاثة التالية: أولها: العقل وذلك في مثل قوله تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ فِي ذَلِكَ لَذِكْرَى لِمَنْ كَانَ لَهُ قَلْب﴾ [ق: ٣٧/٥٠]. الثاني: بمعنى الرأي والتدبير، وذلك في مثل قوله تعالى: ﴿تَحْسَبُهُمْ جَمِيعاً وَقُلُوبُهُمْ شَتّى﴾ [الحشر: ١٤/٥٩]. الثالث: بمعنى حقيقة القلب الذي في الصدر، وذلك في مثل قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَكِنْ تَعْمَى الْقُلُوبُ الَّتِي فِي الصُّدُور﴾ [الحج: ٤٦/٢٢]. وهذا المعنى الثالث إنما يشير إلى الجانب الوظيفي للعقل. فكما أن البصر اسم للإدراك التام الكامل الحاصل بالعين التي في الرأس؛ فالبصيرة اسم للإدراك التام الحاصل في القلب. قال تعالى: ﴿بَلِ الإِنْسَانُ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ بَصِيرَةٌ﴾ [القيامة: ١٤/٧٥]، أي له بنفسه معرفة تامة. أي أن العقل يستخدم في القرآن باعتباره موضعاً للعلم والمعرفة. أَفَلا يَتَدَبَّرُونَ الْقُرْآنَ أَمْ عَلَى قُلُوبٍ أَقْفَالُهَا [محمد: ٢٤/٤٧]. ووفق هذا المعنى فإن القلب في نظر القرآن أداة من أدوات المعرفة، حيث يعتمد القرآن على مخاطبة القلب في معظم رسالته. ومثل هذا الاستنتاج مما قد يُشكل استيعابه بالنظر إلى الشائع من كون العقل وظيفته الإرادة في حين أن القلب وظيفته العاطفة ولكن اهتمام القرآن الواضح بالقلب إلى حد احتوائه ١٢٢ آيةً تتحدث عنه بجوانبه المختلفة، بحيث تتعـدد صوره، فتارة نشعر أننا أمام صورة العقل ذاته، وتارة نشعر أننا أمام العاطفة والمشاعر الوجدانية، وثالثة نشعر أننا أمام الجانبين معاً: جانب العقل وجانب العاطفة وهكذا. ذلك كله مما يساعد على إزالة ذلك الإشكال المفترض. ونتيجة لذكر القلب في القرآن بوصفه اسم جنس مفرداً ومجموعاً، بخلاف العقل الذي ورد مفرداً مشتقاً من اسم جنسه، فإن ذلك دفع ببعض الباحثين لاستخلاص أن ليس هناك شئ مجسّم في جسم الإنسان، لذات اسمه العقل. أما القلب فإن هناك شيئاً لذات اسمه القلب وهو تلك المضغة القائمة في الصدر. الأمر الذي يدعونا للفصل التام بين كل من العقل والقلب، لنصل إلى أن القلب من الألفاظ المشتركة في معانيها، وأن من جملة تلك المعاني (العقل).
The heart occurs in the Quran with one of the following three meanings: First: intellect, as in His statement, the Most High: 'Indeed in that is a reminder for whoever has a heart' [Qaf 50:37]. Second: meaning opinion and management, as in His statement, the Most High: 'You think they are united, but their hearts are diverse' [al-Hashr 59:14]. Third: meaning the reality of the heart that is in the chest, as in His statement, the Most High: 'But blind are the hearts that are in the chests' [al-Hajj 22:46]. This third meaning refers to the functional aspect of the intellect. For just as sight is the name for complete and perfect perception obtained by the eye in the head, so insight (basira) is the name for complete perception obtained in the heart. He, the Most High, said: 'Rather, man against himself is insight' [al-Qiyama 75:14], meaning he has complete knowledge of himself. That is, the intellect is used in the Quran as a locus of knowledge and cognition. 'Then do they not reflect upon the Quran, or are there locks upon their hearts?' [Muhammad 47:24]. According to this meaning, the heart in the view of the Quran is an instrument of knowledge, as the Quran relies on addressing the heart in most of its message. This conclusion may be difficult to comprehend given the common notion that the intellect's function is will while the heart's function is emotion, but the Quran's clear emphasis on the heart to the extent that it contains 122 verses speaking about its various aspects, such that its images multiply: sometimes we feel we are facing the image of the intellect itself, sometimes we feel we are facing emotion and sentimental feelings, and a third time we feel we are facing both aspects together: the aspect of intellect and the aspect of emotion, and so on. All of this helps remove that supposed difficulty. As a result of mentioning the heart in the Quran as a generic noun, singular and plural, unlike the intellect which appeared singularly derived from its generic noun, this led some researchers to conclude that there is no bodily thing in the human body with the essence named intellect. As for the heart, there is something with the essence named the heart, which is that piece of flesh located in the chest. This necessitates a complete separation between the intellect and the heart, leading us to the conclusion that the heart is among the polysemous words in its meanings, and that among those meanings is (the intellect).
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage classifies the Quranic meanings of 'qalb' (heart) and relates it to intellect ('aql) as an epistemological tool. The author begins by listing three distinct meanings: (1) intellect itself, citing Quran 50:37 where having a heart implies understanding; (2) opinion and management, as in Quran 59:14 where hearts are described as scattered; (3) the physical organ in the chest, from Quran 22:46 which speaks of blindness of hearts. The third meaning is then explained functionally: just as physical sight (basar) is perception via the eye, insight (basira) is perception via the heart, citing Quran 75:14. Thus the intellect in the Quran is a locus of knowledge, as confirmed by Quran 47:24 questioning whether hearts are locked. The author addresses a common misconception—that intellect is about will and heart about emotion—by showing that the Quran's extensive use of 'heart' (122 verses) encompasses intellect, emotion, and both together. Finally, the author notes that linguistically 'aql appears only as a singular derivative, while 'qalb' appears as a generic noun in singular and plural, leading some researchers to conclude that 'aql has no physical counterpart whereas 'qalb does (the flesh in the chest). Therefore 'qalb' is a homonym including the meaning of intellect, but the physical heart is something else. This analysis uses purely Quranic evidence and traditional lexicography, grounding epistemology in revelation.

العقل
الرأي والتدبير

Key Takeaway
The Quran uses 'qalb' as a homonym, with its first meaning being intellect, demonstrating that the heart is primarily an epistemic organ.

The Heart as an Instrument of Knowledge in the Quran
Author discusses heart as knowledge instrument and resolves misconception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the heart functions as an epistemological instrument in the Quran, resolving the apparent conflict between intellect and emotion.

Core Idea
In the Quran, the heart is the seat of both intellect and emotion, merging reason and feeling in one cognitive organ.

The passage argues that the heart is not merely an emotional center but a primary instrument of knowledge. This lesson unpacks the Quranic concept of basira (insight) and the functional role of the heart in acquiring knowledge, addressing the common misconception that intellect and heart are separate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the functional analogy
The author compares sight (basar) to insight (basira). Note that physical perception via the eye is paralleled by inner perception via the heart.
This analogy is crucial for understanding the heart's cognitive role.
2
Locate the Quranic evidence for basira
Find the verse al-Qiyama 75:14 and understand its implication: man has complete knowledge of himself through his heart (basira).
3
Analyze the relationship between 'aql and qalb
The passage states that 'aql is used in the Quran as a locus of knowledge, and it resides in the heart. Note the linguistic observation that 'aql appears only as a derivative while qalb appears as a generic noun.
This shows that the heart is the substrate for intellect.
4
Resolve the common misconception
The author acknowledges that some think intellect is about will and heart about emotion. Show how the Quran's 122 verses about the heart encompass both, thereby removing the difficulty.
