الباب الثالث: الفصل الرابع - المصادر التبعية
والواقع أن هذا المثال ينطبق بدرجة أكبر على الحدس، لأن حدسك هو الذي أوحى إليك بأن هذا إنسان غير جيد، ولا يستحق أن تمنحه صداقتك، ذلك أن عاملي التنبؤ والترقب قائمان فيه، فأنت – في حقيقة الأمر – إنما من صدق شعورك في النفور الخفي منه بعد مرور فترة غير قصيرة حسبما جاء في المثال المفترض، وذلك ما يتصف به الحدس وليس الإلهام عنـد التحقيق في دقائق صفات كل منهما.
تحققت
وفي ختام الحديث عن مدى العلاقة بين الحدس والإلهام يحسن أن أؤكد على أنه بالرغم من عدم الإقرار بهذا الترادف بينهما إلا أنه لا يسع الباحث في هذا الإطار إنكار أو إغفال أن ثمة ترابطًا - حسبما يرى بعض الباحثين – بين الحدس والإلهام من حيث إن كليهما يتم عن طريق الإدراك الباطني الذوقي والوجداني المباشر (۱) . وسمته أن يُقذف في القلب بسرعة خاطفة كما لو كان شعاع نور).
علاقة الإلهام بالعقل والحواس
يذهب بعض الباحثين إلى أن الإلهام عملية قلبية تتمثل في أن الإنسان قد يحس بقلبه ما لا يحس بعقله، تماما كما أنه قد يدرك بعقله ما لا يدرك بقلبه فلكل منهما خصوصية، فإذا كان العقل متميزاً بالمنطقية المتسلسلة ذات الاستدلال، فإن القلب فجائي ومباشر وإلهامي واضح. ولذلك فإن المقصود بالقلب هنا المعنوي لا المادي، وهو ذلك الذي قد يشعر المرء بحقيقته في نفسه دون أن يجد دليلاً منطقيًا على فكرة ما، لكنه لا يقتنع بها قلبيًا (۳).
ولنا أن نتساءل هل حقا هذه هي طبيعة العلاقة التي تحكم القلب بالإلهام؟ والجواب نسترجعه من منزلة هذه المصادر التي قلنا عنها في أول الحديث إنها تبعية ثانوية، ولابد أن تجد لها سنداً من واحد من المصادر والطرائق الرئيسة للمعرفة وهي: الوحي أو العقل أو الحس. وهذا هو جوهر الفرق بينها وبين ما بالكشف والذوق وسواهما. ولذلك فإن أياً من الحدس أو الإلهام أو الرؤيا الصالحة لا تمتلك القوة ذاتها التي تمتلكها المصادر والطرائق الرئيسة أو أي واحد منها. وبناءً على هذا فإن من غير المسلّم به القول بأن القلب المعنوي قـد لصاحبه بحقيقة ما لا يجد عليها دليلاً منطقياً من القلب المادي والعكس! ذلك لأن تقديم الموضوع بهذا القالب يتضمن نتيجة منطقية هي أنه لا لقاء بين الإلهام والعقل أو أن وجود الإلهام يقتضي إقصاء العقل والعكس صحيح وعلاوة على أنه لا مستند لهذا الفصل غير الموضوعي بين القلب وتشطيره إلى معنوي ومادي فإنه لن يوصل إلا إلى نتيجة غير موضوعية، ربما لم تكن لتخطر يبال أولئك الذين نحوا هذا المنحى، وهي تلك اللوازم السابقة. وهنا يجب التفريق بين حصول الإلهام فجأة من غير مقدمات منطقية، وبين مصادمته لبراهين العقل أو نتائجه الراجحة، فالأولى سمة أساسية في الإلهام، في حين أن الثانية مجرد خاطر عابر لا يلتفت إليه.
وقد عزا الإمام الغزالي حصول الإلهام أو الحدس - كعادته في عدم التفريق بينهما - إلى العقل الفعّال (۱) ، وردّ على من يشتبه عليه الأمر في كون هذه القوة موجودة في غير النبي، ومن ثم فليست خاصية له بأن عقل النبي فوق العقول كلّها (۲).
Chapter Three: Section Four - Subsidiary Sources
In reality, this example applies to a greater degree to intuition, because your intuition is what inspired you that this person is not good and does not deserve your friendship, since the factors of prediction and anticipation are present in it. You – in truth – only trusted your feeling of hidden aversion after a not-short period as in the supposed example, and that is what characterizes intuition and not inspiration when investigating the subtleties of the attributes of each.
And at the conclusion of the discussion about the extent of the relationship between intuition and inspiration, it is good to emphasize that despite the lack of acknowledgment of synonymity between them, a researcher in this framework cannot deny or overlook that there is a connection – according to some researchers – between intuition and inspiration in that both occur through inner, taste-based, and immediate emotional perception. And its description is that it is cast into the heart with swiftness as if it were a ray of light.
The relationship of inspiration to reason and the senses
Some researchers hold that inspiration is a heart-based process consisting in that a person may feel with his heart what he does not feel with his mind, just as he may perceive with his mind what he does not perceive with his heart; each has its specificity. If reason is distinguished by sequential logic with inference, then the heart is sudden, direct, and clearly inspirational. Therefore, what is meant by the heart here is the spiritual heart, not the physical, and it is that which a person may feel its reality in himself without finding a logical proof for an idea, but he is not convinced by it heartily.
We may ask: Is this truly the nature of the relationship that governs the heart with inspiration? The answer we retrieve from the status of these sources that we said at the beginning of the discussion are subsidiary and secondary; they must find support from one of the main sources and methods of knowledge, namely: revelation, reason, or sense. This is the essence of the difference between them and what is through unveiling, taste, and others. Therefore, none of intuition, inspiration, or a righteous dream possesses the same strength that the main sources and methods possess or any one of them. And based on this, it is not acceptable to say that the spiritual heart may befriend a person with a truth for which he finds no logical proof from the physical heart and vice versa! That is because presenting the subject in this mold entails a logical conclusion that there is no meeting between inspiration and reason, or that the existence of inspiration necessitates the exclusion of reason and vice versa. Moreover, there is no basis for this non-objective separation between the heart and its division into spiritual and physical, it will only lead to a non-objective result, perhaps not contemplated by those who took this path, namely those previous implications. Here we must distinguish between the occurrence of inspiration suddenly without logical premises, and its collision with rational proofs or their preponderant conclusions; the first is an essential characteristic of inspiration, while the second is just a passing thought that is not heeded.
And Imam al-Ghazali attributed the occurrence of inspiration or intuition – as was his habit in not distinguishing between them – to the active intellect, and he responded to those who doubted that this power exists in other than the Prophet, and therefore it is not exclusive to him, even though the intellect of the Prophet is above all intellects.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological discussion about two subsidiary sources of knowledge: intuition (hads) and inspiration (ilham). The author begins by distinguishing them through an example: intuition involves prediction and anticipation based on subtle feelings over time, while inspiration is a sudden direct casting into the heart. Despite differences, they share a connection through inner, taste-based, immediate perception. The author then examines the relationship of inspiration to reason and the senses. Some researchers claim that inspiration is a heart process independent of reason, and that the heart here is the spiritual heart, not the physical. The author questions this by recalling that these sources are subsidiary and must ultimately rely on one of the primary sources: revelation, reason, or senses. Thus, neither intuition, inspiration, nor dreams have independent authority; they require support. The author then critiques the division of the heart into spiritual and physical, arguing that it leads to a false dichotomy that seems to separate inspiration and reason. Instead, one must distinguish between inspiration coming suddenly without logical premises (a characteristic) and its contradiction of rational proofs (which is dismissed as a passing thought). Finally, the author notes that al-Ghazali attributed both inspiration and intuition to the active intellect and affirmed that the Prophet's intellect is superior, but the power itself is not exclusive to prophets. The passage guards against overvaluing inspiration or intuition as independent sources of knowledge.

Key Terms
الحدس
الإلهام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is a key difference between intuition (hads) and inspiration (ilham)?
A) Intuition is sudden; inspiration is gradual.
B) Intuition involves prediction and time; inspiration is sudden and direct.
C) Both are identical in nature.
D) Inspiration is from the mind; intuition from the heart.

Key Takeaway
Intuition is predictive and time-dependent; inspiration is sudden and direct; both require support from primary sources.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider a scenario: A student of knowledge feels an immediate, strong inner conviction that a certain interpretation of a verse is correct, without any prior reasoning or evidence. Is this an example of hads or ilham? Justify your answer using the passage's criteria.
?
Find a real or hypothetical claim from a contemporary speaker that invokes 'divine inspiration' for a religious ruling. Evaluate whether the description fits the passage's definition of ilham, and discuss what additional validation would be required.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq

Epistemological Critique of Independent Inspiration
Author critiques the independence of inspiration from reason and reaffirms subsidiary sources' dependence on primary sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to critique the claim that inspiration is independent of reason and explain why subsidiary sources must rely on primary sources of knowledge.

Core Idea
Inspiration is not an independent source; it must lean on revelation, reason, or senses.

In the second part of the passage, the author addresses a controversial view: that inspiration is a heart-based process independent of reason, with a spiritual heart separate from the physical one. The author deconstructs this view, showing it leads to a false dichotomy and undermines the subsidiary nature of inspiration. This lesson unpacks his critique.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being critiqued
Some researchers hold that inspiration is a heart process where one feels with the heart what the mind does not, and they distinguish a spiritual heart from the physical heart.
The claim implies a separation between heart-based inspiration and rational inference.
2
Extract the author's counter-argument
The author argues that such a division leads to the logical conclusion that inspiration and reason are mutually exclusive, which is non-objective. He also asserts that these sources are subsidiary and must be supported by primary sources: revelation, reason, or senses.
The author uses the subsidiary status to undercut the claim of independence.
3
Understand the key distinction
The author distinguishes between inspiration occurring suddenly (its essential characteristic) and inspiration contradicting rational proofs (which is dismissed as a passing thought).
This protects inspiration from being used to overturn established rational knowledge.
4
Recognize the role of primary sources
Subsidiary sources like inspiration and intuition do not possess independent authority; they must find a basis in one of the primary sources.
This preserves the epistemological hierarchy and prevents misuse.

Ilham as a Secondary Source: Critique and Conditions
Author critiques inspiration and sets conditions for its acceptance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why inspiration lacks certainty and list the conditions under which it becomes acceptable according to Ibn al-Sam'ani.

Core Idea
Inspiration is uncertain until verified by Shari'a.

In this passage, the author critically examines inspiration (ilham) as a source of knowledge. He argues that it lacks epistemic certainty because its origin cannot be determined. However, drawing on Ibn al-Sam'ani, he outlines how inspiration can be conditionally accepted if it aligns with the Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three possible origins of inspiration
From the text: inspiration may come from God, Satan, or the self. This uncertainty is why it cannot be trusted without verification.
This is the core epistemological problem.
2
Understand why inspiration lacks certainty
Because we cannot verify its source, inspiration only yields probability (zann), not certainty (yaqin). It offers no demonstrative proof (burhan).
The author uses terms like 'expectation or probability'.
3
Extract the condition for acceptance from Ibn al-Sam'ani
Inspiration is accepted only if it is consistent with the Muhammadan Shari'a (Quran and Sunnah) and nothing contradicts it. Otherwise, it is rejected as self-talk or devilish whispering.
This is a key condition: agreement with revelation.
4
Determine when inspiration can be acted upon
The majority view: inspiration is not a legal proof (hujja shar'iyya) and is acted upon only when all other proofs are absent, and only in matters of the permissible (mubah).
This limits its scope significantly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن هنا فإن الإلهام، وإن مثل مصدراً للمعرفة وفق التفصيل السابق، إلا أنه لا يمتلك هذه الصفة من الناحية الواقعية، وذلك من حيث الثقة بما يقدمه، فلا يقينية فيه لعدم معرفتنا هل هذه المصدرية حقاً من الله؟ أم من الشيطان؟ أم من النفس، وعليه فإنها فردية مختصة بالشخص المدعي لها وحده، ولا يمتلك سلطة برهانية تقنع غيره بيقينية دعواه ،وصدقها، ومن ثم فلا يعدو ما تقدمه التوقع أو الاحتمال لا العلم) .
ويلخص ابن السمعاني (ت: ٤٨٩ هـ هذا الأمر أحسن تلخيص إذ يقول: وإنكار الإلهام ،مردود، ويجوز أن يفعل الله بعبده ما يكرهه به ولكن التمييز بين الحق والباطل في ذلك؛ أن كل ما استقام على الشريعة المحمدية، ولم يكن في الكتاب والسنة ما يردّه فهو مقبول، وإلا فمردود يقع من حديث النفس ووسوسة الشيطان، ثم قال: ونحن لا ننكر أن الله يكرم عبده بزيادة نور منه یزداد به نظره ويقوى به رأيه، وإنما ننكر أن يرجع إلى قلبه بقول لا يعرف أصله، ولا نزعم أنه حجّة شرعية، وإنما هو نور يختص الله به من يشاء من عباده، فإن وافق الشرع كان الحجّة (۲) .
ونخبة القول: إن الجمهور لا يجيز العمل بالإلهام إلا عند فقدان الحجج كلها في باب المباح). ولذلك فليس سائغاً أن تعتمد مناهج التربية الإسلامية على (الإلهام) في تقرير حقائق أو إصدار أحكام قطعية، ولكنها تسعى لتنمية هذا المصدر لدى المتعلمين بجملة موجهات عقدية وسلوكية تسهم في الارتقاء بمستوياتهم الذهنية لبلوغ درجة الإلهام، مع تجنب بعض التوجيهات التي تفضي إلى بلوغ حالة من (الدروشة والتي هي أقرب إلى التفكير الخرافي منها إلى الإلهام وفق منهج التفكير العلمي. ولكن المربي المسلم يمكنه الحرص على تزكية نفس المتعلم من خلال عناصر نسق التعلم الإسلامي الذي يهتم بالتعبد والنوافل والتقوى والورع، على النحو الذي يُفجر الطاقات الداخلية للمتعلم المسلم بما يعزز نموه المعرفي، إلى جانب مهارة التحقيق المعرفي لنتائج التعلم.

الإلهام والتفكير العلمي
وثمة سؤال منطقي ينشأ هنا وهو: ألا يقع قدر من التعارض كبيراً كان أو صغيراً عند إقرار مصدرية ثانوية للمعرفة هي الإلهام، خاصة حينما يساند ذلــك القرآن الكريم ومنهج التفكير العلمي؟.
والحق أن التعارض بين الإلهام ومنهج التفكير العلمي منتف، أو هو مما لا وجود له أساساً بينهما. ومن هذا الباب جاءت مساندة القرآن الكريم للإلهام وفق القيود المشار إليها سلفاً.
وليس مما يقلل من أهمية هذا المصدر كونه لم يقع تحت نظرية اختبارية أو عقلية نتيجة طريقتها التي تجعل من الاتصال الداخلي بين الإنسان والحقيقة الكونية أو (الله) أو عالم الأرواح مبنية على نوع من التخاطب الروحي بين الفرد وبين الكائنات الروحية بشرية كانت أو ذات وجود أولي مستقل(۱). وكون منهج التفكير العلمي لا يملك تفسيراً محدداً لمصدرية الإلهام فليس ذلك دليلاً على أن الإلهام ليس منهجاً علمياً.
إن منهج التفكير العلمي يقف اليوم عاجزاً أمام ظواهر شتى لا يجد لهـا تفسيراً علمياً تجريبياً أو عقلياً، ولكنه في الوقت ذاته لا يملك إلا إعلان العجز حالياً، والاستعداد لمزيد من البحث مستقبلاً.
Hence, inspiration, although it is represented as a source of knowledge according to the previous detail, yet it does not possess this quality from a realistic perspective, that is, in terms of trust in what it presents. There is no certainty in it because we do not know whether this source is truly from God, or from Satan, or from the self. Accordingly, it is individual, specific to the person who claims it alone, and it does not possess demonstrative authority to convince others of the certainty of his claim and its truth. Hence what it provides is nothing more than expectation or probability, not knowledge. Ibn al-Sam'ani (d. 489 AH) summarized this matter excellently when he said: Denial of inspiration is rejected, and it is permissible for God to do with His servant what He wills. But the distinction between truth and falsehood in that is: everything that is consistent with the Muhammadan Shari'a, and there is nothing in the Book and the Sunnah that rejects it, is acceptable; otherwise it is rejected and comes from self-talk and the whispering of Satan. Then he said: We do not deny that God honors His servant with an increase of light from Him by which his insight increases and his opinion strengthens. Rather, we deny that something returns to his heart as a statement whose origin is unknown. And we do not claim that it is a legal proof; rather, it is a light that God singles out whom He wills of His servants. If it agrees with the Shari'a, then it becomes the proof. And the cream of the statement: The majority does not permit acting upon inspiration except when all proofs are absent in matters of the permissible. Therefore, it is not permissible for Islamic education curricula to rely on inspiration in establishing truths or issuing decisive judgments. Rather, they seek to develop this source among learners through a set of creedal and behavioral directives that contribute to raising their intellectual levels to reach the degree of inspiration, while avoiding some directives that lead to a state of 'dervishness' which is closer to superstitious thinking than to inspiration according to the method of scientific thinking. But the Muslim educator can ensure the purification of the learner's soul through the elements of the Islamic learning system that cares for worship, supererogatory acts, piety, and scrupulousness, in a way that unleashes the internal energies of the Muslim learner, enhancing his cognitive growth, along with the skill of cognitive verification of learning outcomes. Inspiration and Scientific Thinking There arises a logical question here: Does there not occur a degree of conflict, whether large or small, when acknowledging a secondary source of knowledge which is inspiration, especially when the Noble Quran and the method of scientific thinking support that? The truth is that the conflict between inspiration and the method of scientific thinking is non-existent, or rather there is no basis for it between them. From this perspective came the Quran's support for inspiration according to the previously mentioned restrictions. Nor does its importance diminish because it has not fallen under an experimental or rational theory due to its method that makes the internal connection between man and the cosmic reality or (God) or the world of spirits based on a kind of spiritual communication between the individual and spiritual beings, whether human or having an independent primal existence. And the fact that the method of scientific thinking does not have a specific explanation for the source of inspiration is not evidence that inspiration is not a scientific method. The method of scientific thinking today stands helpless before various phenomena for which it finds no empirical or rational scientific explanation, but at the same time it can only declare helplessness currently and prepare for more research in the future.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological critique of inspiration (ilham) as a source of knowledge, followed by conditions for its acceptance and a defense of its compatibility with scientific thinking. The author begins by stating that despite previous discussion classifying inspiration as a secondary source, it lacks real epistemic authority because it is not certain. The reason is that we cannot verify its origin—whether from God, Satan, or the self. Therefore, it remains individual and non-demonstrative, offering only probability, not knowledge. The author then quotes Ibn al-Sam'ani, who affirms that inspiration is not to be denied but must be tested against the Shari'a. If it agrees with the Quran and Sunnah, it is accepted; otherwise it is rejected as self-talk or devilish whispering. Ibn al-Sam'ani clarifies that inspiration is not a 'legal proof' but a light from God; if it aligns with Shari'a, it becomes a proof. The author then summarizes the majority view: inspiration is only acted upon when all other proofs are absent, and only in matters of the permissible (mubah). Consequently, Islamic education cannot base decisive truths on inspiration, but can nurture it through spiritual and behavioral development, avoiding superstitious states. The passage then addresses the potential conflict with scientific thinking. The author asserts there is no conflict; the Quran supports inspiration under the given restrictions. The fact that inspiration is not subject to experimental or rational methods does not diminish its value. Scientific method itself is helpless before many phenomena and can only acknowledge its current limitations. Thus, inspiration remains a valid (though secondary) source, provided it is filtered through Shari'a.

Key Terms
الإلهام
مصدرية تبعية
حجّة شرعية
برهان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is inspiration considered acceptable?
A) Always, because it comes from God.
B) Only when it agrees with the Quran and Sunnah and nothing contradicts it.
C) Only in matters of the obligatory (wajib).
D) Never, because it is always from Satan.

Key Takeaway
Inspiration is not a certain source of knowledge; its acceptance depends on agreement with Shari'a and is limited to cases where other proofs are absent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider a claim of inspiration in your own context (e.g., a dream suggesting a ruling). Using Ibn al-Sam'ani's condition, explain whether this inspiration would be accepted or rejected.
?
Identify a secondary source of knowledge in Islamic jurisprudence (e.g., qiyas, istihsan) and explain how its epistemic status is similar to or different from ilham as described here.

Tasawwur and Tasdiq
advanced
8 min
Reconciling Inspiration with Scientific Thinking
Author reconciles inspiration with scientific thinking.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the author's argument that there is no conflict between inspiration and scientific thinking, and evaluate its strength.

Core Idea
Inspiration and scientific method need not conflict; both have limits.

The passage anticipates a logical question: does acknowledging inspiration contradict scientific thinking? The author argues that there is no conflict, citing the Quran's support and the limitations of scientific method. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the potential conflict the author addresses
The author asks whether acknowledging inspiration as a secondary source contradicts the Quran and scientific thinking, especially since the Quran supports both.
The conflict is only apparent.
2
Extract the author's response
The author asserts there is no conflict. The Quran itself supports inspiration under the given restrictions.
3
Analyze the author's justification
The author argues that the scientific method cannot explain everything. Its failure to account for inspiration does not mean inspiration is invalid. Scientific thinking itself acknowledges its limits.
This is a defense of inspiration's epistemic value.
4
Evaluate the argument's strength
Consider whether the analogy between scientific helplessness and acceptability of inspiration is sound. Does the author provide positive evidence for inspiration?
Critical thinking: the argument avoids the charge of contradiction but does not prove inspiration's reliability.

According to the passage, what is the relationship between inspiration and scientific thinking?
A) They are in direct conflict, and one must choose.

Definition and Levels of True Visions
Author defines ru'ya linguistically and terminologically, then distinguishes its two levels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between general and specific definitions of ru'ya and identify the two levels of true visions with their epistemological status.

Core Idea
True visions: secondary source for believers, primary for prophets as revelation.

In this lesson, we explore the concept of true visions (al-ru'ya al-sadiqa) as a source of knowledge in Islam. The author defines ru'ya linguistically and terminologically, then distinguishes between ordinary dreams and true visions that come true for believers. He further elevates the visions of prophets to the level of revelation, making them a primary source.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish linguistic and terminological definitions
Note the root 'ra'a' (to see in sleep) and how the author moves to the technical term. The general definition includes any sleeper's dreams that may or may not reflect the future.
2
Extract the specific definition of true visions
Find the restriction to believers and the condition of vivid reflection like the break of dawn. This is the secondary source of knowledge for believers.
Contrast with 'adghath al-ahlam' (jumbled dreams).
3
Identify the two levels of ru'ya
The author explicitly divides ru'ya into the level of prophets and the level of common truthful believers.
4
Analyze the epistemological distinction
Understand why prophets' ru'ya is primary (derived directly from waḥy) while believers' is secondary. Use the story of Joseph (Yusuf) as evidence.
Prophets' ru'ya does not exit the sphere of revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثالث: الفصل الرابع - المصادر التبعية
وبصورة عامة فإن الانعكاسات التربوية المباشرة للإلهام لا تخرج في مجملها عن انعكاسات الحدس، سواء في ذلك ركائز الفلسفة التربوية، أو عناصر المنهاج، أو المعلم والمتعلم، وذلك من حيث إنهما (الحدس والإلهام مصادر ثانوية غير مكتسبة بالتربية النظامية كما قلنا عند الحديث عن الحدس . وإذا كان ثمة فرق جوهري بينهما فهو أن المتعلم المسلم يفترض فيه يسعى لتحقيق نسق التعلم الإسلامي الذي أشرنا إليه من قبل، وهو الذي يفضي بالمتعلم إلى بلوغ مرتبة الإلهام، ومن ثم الحصول على مصدريته.

ثالثاً - الرؤيا الصادقة
تعريف الرؤيا
الرؤيا في اللغة مأخوذة من رأى في منامه (رؤيا) على فعلـى بـلا تنوين. والجمع رؤى بالتنوين بوزن رعی(۱).
وفي الاصطلاح يمكن تقسيم التعريف إلى معنى عام وآخر خاص. فالرؤيا بصورة عامة ما يراه النائم في منامه من أحداث وصور ومواقف قد تنعكس في مستقبل أيامه بما يحب ويكره.
وقولنا (النائم) في هذا التعريف إشارة إلى أنها عامة في كـل نـائـم مـن غـيـر تخصيص لها بدين له أو بمستوى من التدين عنده أما أنها قد تنعكس، فإن في ذلك إشارة أيضاً إلى أنها قد لا تنعكس بالضرورة في مستقبل أيام الرائي، وهذا ما يُعرف بأضغاث الأحلام، وهذا هو مقصودنا بالمعنى الخاص، أي ما يراه المؤمن في منامه من أحداث وصور ومواقف تنعكس في مستقبل أيامه فيما يحب ويكره، وتأتي كفلق الصبح لشدة وضوحها، فالتقييد لـهـا بالمؤمن يُخرج من من الناس، لأنها تشكل بالنسبة إليه واحداً من مصادر المعرفة التبعية عداه

مستويات الرؤيا الصادقة
هناك مستويات من الرؤيا: مستوى الرؤيا في حق الأنبياء - عليهم السلام- ومستوى الرؤيا في حق عموم المؤمنين الصادقين. وذلك يستلزم إيضاحاً على النحو التالي:
المستوى الأول: مستوى الرؤيا في حق الأنبياء - عليهم السلام - وهذا المستوى يرقى إلى مستوى المصادر الرئيسة، إذ إنه لا يمثل مجرد مصدر ثانوي للمعرفة لكونه مستمداً من الوحي مباشرة، فرؤيا الأنبياء لا تخرج عن دائرة الوحي(۱).
ومن ذلك - على سبيل المثال ما جاء في قصة يوسف- عليه السلام- وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿قالَ يُوسُفُ لأَبِيهِ يا أَبَتِ إِنِّي رَأَيْتُ أَحَدَ عَشَرَ كَوْكَبَاً وَالشَّمْسَ وَالْقَمَرَ رَأَيْتُهُمْ لِي سَاجِدِينَ ﴾ [يوسف: ٤/١٢].
وبعد نهاية محنة يوسف قال لأبيه: ﴿وَقالَ يا أَبَتِ هَذا تَأْوِيلُ رُؤْيَايَ ﴾ [يوسف: ١٠٠/١٢].
وقال يوسف أيضاً في سياق تفسيره لرؤيا السجينين إن تفسيره من وحي الله له: قالَ لا يَأْتِيكُما طَعَامٌ تُرْزَقَانِهِ إِلا نَبَّأتكما بتأويلِهِ قَبْلَ أَن يَأْتِيَكُما ذَلِكُما مِمَّا عَلْمَنِي رَبِّي... [يوسف: ٣٧/١٢].
Chapter Three: Section Four - Secondary Sources
And in general, the direct educational reflections of inspiration do not differ in their entirety from the reflections of intuition, both in the foundations of educational philosophy, the elements of the curriculum, and the teacher and learner, insofar as they (intuition and inspiration) are secondary sources not acquired through formal education as we said when discussing intuition. And if there is a fundamental difference between them, it is that the Muslim learner is supposed to strive to achieve the Islamic learning pattern which we indicated previously, and which leads the learner to attain the level of inspiration, and thereby obtain its source-status.

Thirdly: True Visions (Ru'ya)
Definition of Ru'ya
Linguistically, ru'ya is derived from 'ra'a' (he saw) in his sleep, taking the form 'ru'ya' (رؤيا) without tanween. The plural is 'ru'an' with tanween, on the meter of 'ru'an' (رؤى).
Terminologically, the definition can be divided into a general meaning and a specific meaning. Ru'ya in general terms is what the sleeping person sees in his sleep of events, images, and situations that may reflect in the future of his days, whether he likes or dislikes them.
Our saying 'the sleeping person' in this definition indicates that it is general for every sleeper, without specifying a particular religion or level of religiosity. And our saying 'may reflect' also indicates that they may not necessarily reflect in the future of the dreamer's days, and this is known as 'adghath al-ahlam' (jumbled dreams). And this is our intended meaning in the specific sense: that is, what the believer sees in his sleep of events, images, and situations that reflect in the future of his days, in what he likes or dislikes, coming like the break of dawn due to their vividness. Thus, restricting it to the believer excludes others, because it constitutes for him one of the secondary sources of knowledge.

Levels of True Visions
There are levels of ru'ya: the level of ru'ya for the prophets - peace be upon them - and the level of ru'ya for the common truthful believers. This requires clarification as follows:
The first level: the level of ru'ya for the prophets - peace be upon them. This level rises to the level of primary sources, for it is not merely a secondary source of knowledge, being derived directly from revelation. The ru'ya of the prophets does not exit the sphere of revelation.
An example of that is what is mentioned in the story of Joseph - peace be upon him - namely His statement, the Exalted: 'Joseph said to his father, O my father, indeed I have seen eleven stars and the sun and the moon; I saw them prostrating to me.' [Yusuf 12:4]
And after the end of Joseph's ordeal, he said to his father: 'And he said, O my father, this is the interpretation of my vision of before.' [Yusuf 12:100]
And Joseph also said in the context of his interpretation of the dream of the two prisoners that his interpretation is from God's revelation to him: 'He said, There will not come to you any food which you are provided with except that I will inform you of its interpretation before it comes to you. That is from what my Lord has taught me.' [Yusuf 12:37]
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage defines 'al-ru'ya al-sadiqa' (true visions) as a secondary source of knowledge in Islamic epistemology, and distinguishes its two levels. The author begins by noting that inspiration (ilhām) and intuition (hads) are secondary sources; then introduces true visions as a third secondary source. 

The definition is given first linguistically: ru'ya is derived from 'ra'a' (to see in sleep). Then terminologically, it is divided into general and specific. The general definition covers any sleeper's dreams that may or may not come true. The specific definition restricts true visions to believers: they are vivid dreams that inevitably come true, like the break of dawn. This specific ru'ya is a secondary source of knowledge for believers.

Next, the author discusses levels of true visions. There are two levels: the ru'ya of prophets and that of ordinary truthful believers. The prophets' ru'ya is not secondary but primary, because it is derived directly from revelation (waḥy). It does not exit the sphere of revelation. Proof is given from the story of Prophet Joseph (Yusuf): his initial dream of eleven stars, the sun, and the moon, and his later interpretation of the prisoners' dreams, which he attributes to God's teaching. Thus, for prophets, ru'ya is subsumed under revelation, making it a primary source of knowledge.

Key Terms
الرؤيا الصادقة
أضغاث الأحلام
الوحي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes prophets' ru'ya from that of ordinary believers?
A) Prophets do not experience ru'ya.
B) Prophets' ru'ya is a primary source of knowledge because it is derived directly from revelation.
C) Ordinary believers' ru'ya is always true.
D) Prophets' ru'ya cannot be interpreted.

Key Takeaway
True visions are vivid dreams of believers that inevitably come true, serving as a secondary knowledge source, while for prophets they are primary because they are revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using the definition from the passage, determine whether the following dream qualifies as a true vision: A non-Muslim sees a dream that vividly comes true the next day. Explain why or why not.
?
Give an example from the Qur'an (other than the story of Yusuf) where a prophet's vision is treated as revelation.
